It is important to have a strong understanding of these concepts before moving on to more complex systems, as they serve as the building blocks for more advanced topics.



### Subsection: 20.1b Equations of Motion for Two-Degree-of-Freedom Systems



In 2.003, we learned how to derive the equations of motion for single-degree-of-freedom systems. In this course, we will extend that knowledge to two-degree-of-freedom systems. These systems have two independent degrees of freedom, meaning they require two coordinates to fully describe their motion.



To derive the equations of motion for a two-degree-of-freedom system, we use the principle of virtual work. This principle states that the virtual work done by all external forces acting on a system must be equal to the virtual work done by the internal forces. By applying this principle, we can obtain a set of coupled differential equations that describe the motion of the system.



The equations of motion for a two-degree-of-freedom system can be written in matrix form as:



$$

M\ddot{q} + C\dot{q} + Kq = F

$$



where $M$ is the mass matrix, $C$ is the damping matrix, $K$ is the stiffness matrix, $q$ is the vector of generalized coordinates, and $F$ is the vector of external forces.



### Subsection: 20.1c Applications from 2.003



The concepts learned in 2.003 have numerous applications in engineering and other fields. One of the most common applications is in the design and control of mechanical systems, such as robots and vehicles. By understanding the dynamics and control of these systems, engineers can optimize their performance and ensure their stability.



Another application is in the field of aerospace engineering. The principles of dynamics and control are crucial in designing and controlling aircraft, spacecraft, and other aerospace systems. These systems often involve complex dynamics and require precise control to ensure their safety and efficiency.



In addition, the concepts learned in 2.003 can also be applied to other fields, such as economics, biology, and even social sciences. Many systems in these fields can be modeled as dynamic systems and can benefit from the principles of dynamics and control.



Overall, the knowledge gained from 2.003 is essential for understanding and analyzing the behavior of various systems and for designing effective control strategies. It serves as a foundation for further study in the field of dynamics and control, and its applications are vast and diverse.





# Title: Modeling Dynamics and Control II:



## Chapter 20: Vibrations of Two-Degree-of-Freedom Systems:



### Section: 20.2 Plane-motion Kinematics of Rigid Bodies:



### Subsection: 20.2a Understanding Plane-motion Kinematics



In this section, we will build upon the concepts covered in 2.003 and apply them to the study of two-degree-of-freedom systems. Specifically, we will focus on the plane-motion kinematics of rigid bodies, which is essential for understanding the behavior of these systems.



#### 20.2a Overview of Plane-motion Kinematics



Plane-motion kinematics deals with the motion of rigid bodies in a two-dimensional plane. It is a fundamental concept in dynamics and control, as it allows us to analyze the motion of objects without considering the internal forces and deformations within the body.



The motion of a rigid body can be described by its position, velocity, and acceleration. These quantities are related through the equations of motion, which are derived from Newton's laws of motion. In the case of plane-motion, these equations can be simplified to only consider motion in two dimensions.



One important concept in plane-motion kinematics is the kinematic chain, which is a series of rigid bodies connected by joints. The motion of each body in the chain is dependent on the motion of the previous body, and this relationship can be described using kinematic equations.



Another important aspect of plane-motion kinematics is the concept of degrees of freedom. A rigid body in a two-dimensional plane has three degrees of freedom, which can be described by the position and orientation of the body. However, in a two-degree-of-freedom system, there are only two independent degrees of freedom, which can be described by two generalized coordinates.



#### 20.2b Kinematic Equations for Two-Degree-of-Freedom Systems



To understand the motion of a two-degree-of-freedom system, we must first define the generalized coordinates. These coordinates represent the independent degrees of freedom of the system and can be chosen based on the geometry and constraints of the system.



Once the generalized coordinates are defined, we can derive the kinematic equations for the system. These equations describe the relationship between the generalized coordinates, velocities, and accelerations of the system. They are essential for understanding the motion of the system and can be used to derive the equations of motion.



#### 20.2c Applications of Plane-motion Kinematics



The concepts of plane-motion kinematics have many practical applications in engineering and physics. For example, they are used in the design and analysis of mechanical systems, such as robots and vehicles. They are also essential for understanding the motion of particles and rigid bodies in fluid mechanics.



In addition, plane-motion kinematics is crucial for the study of vibrations in two-degree-of-freedom systems. By understanding the kinematics of the system, we can analyze the natural frequencies and mode shapes of the system, which are important for designing control strategies to mitigate vibrations.



#### 20.2d Conclusion



In this section, we have provided an overview of plane-motion kinematics and its importance in the study of two-degree-of-freedom systems. We have discussed the kinematic equations and their applications in engineering and physics. In the next section, we will apply these concepts to the study of vibrations in two-degree-of-freedom systems.





# Title: Modeling Dynamics and Control II:



## Chapter 20: Vibrations of Two-Degree-of-Freedom Systems:



### Section: 20.2 Plane-motion Kinematics of Rigid Bodies:



### Subsection: 20.2b Applications of Plane-motion Kinematics



In the previous section, we discussed the basics of plane-motion kinematics and its importance in understanding the behavior of two-degree-of-freedom systems. In this section, we will explore some of the applications of plane-motion kinematics and how it can be used to analyze and model the dynamics of various systems.



#### 20.2b.1 Visualizing the Rotation of a Spacecraft in Orbit



One of the applications of plane-motion kinematics is in visualizing the rotation of a spacecraft in orbit. This is where Poinsot's construction comes into play. Poinsot's construction is a graphical method for representing the rotation of a rigid body in a two-dimensional plane. It involves drawing an ellipse, known as Poinsot's ellipsoid, which represents the orientation of the body at any given time.



This application is particularly useful in the field of aerospace engineering, where understanding the rotation of spacecraft is crucial for their control and stability. By using Poinsot's construction, engineers can visualize and analyze the motion of a spacecraft in orbit, making it easier to design control systems and predict its behavior.



#### 20.2b.2 Maintaining the Extent of a Moving Set of Points



Another application of plane-motion kinematics is in maintaining the extent of a moving set of points. This is a common problem in factory automation, where a set of points on a moving object must be kept within a certain distance from each other. This can be achieved by using Poinsot's construction to analyze the motion of the object and design control systems to maintain the desired extent.



#### 20.2b.3 Modeling the Motion of a Hispano-Suiza 12M Engine



The Hispano-Suiza 12M engine is a classic example of a two-degree-of-freedom system. It is a V12 aircraft engine that was widely used in the 1930s. By applying plane-motion kinematics, we can model the motion of this engine and analyze its behavior. This can help us understand the dynamics of the engine and make improvements to its design.



#### 20.2b.4 Implementing the HEOM Method for Dynamics and Control



The HEOM (Hierarchical Equations of Motion) method is a popular technique for solving the equations of motion for complex systems. It is based on the concept of plane-motion kinematics and is implemented in various codes, including a version for GPUs developed by David Wilkins and Nike Dattani. This method provides a flexible and efficient way to analyze the dynamics and control of complex systems.



#### 20.2b.5 Generalizing to Continuous-time Extended Kalman Filter



The continuous-time extended Kalman filter is a generalization of the discrete-time extended Kalman filter, which is commonly used in control systems. It is based on the concept of plane-motion kinematics and is used to estimate the state of a system based on noisy measurements. By understanding the kinematics of a system, we can derive the equations for the continuous-time extended Kalman filter and use it to improve the accuracy of our control systems.



In conclusion, plane-motion kinematics is a fundamental concept in dynamics and control, and it has various applications in different fields. By understanding the kinematics of a system, we can model its behavior and design control systems to achieve desired outcomes. This makes it an essential tool for engineers and scientists working with two-degree-of-freedom systems.





# Title: Modeling Dynamics and Control II:



## Chapter 20: Vibrations of Two-Degree-of-Freedom Systems:



### Section: 20.2 Plane-motion Kinematics of Rigid Bodies:



### Subsection: 20.2c Challenges in Plane-motion Kinematics



In the previous section, we discussed the basics of plane-motion kinematics and its applications in understanding the behavior of two-degree-of-freedom systems. However, as with any mathematical model, there are certain challenges that arise when using plane-motion kinematics to analyze and model the dynamics of systems. In this section, we will explore some of these challenges and how they can be addressed.



#### 20.2c.1 Nonlinearities in the System



One of the main challenges in using plane-motion kinematics is dealing with nonlinearities in the system. Nonlinearities can arise due to various factors such as friction, damping, and external forces. These nonlinearities can significantly affect the behavior of the system and make it difficult to accurately model and predict its dynamics.



To address this challenge, various techniques such as linearization and numerical methods can be used. Linearization involves approximating the nonlinear system with a linear one, making it easier to analyze and model. Numerical methods, on the other hand, involve using computational tools to solve the equations of motion for the system, taking into account the nonlinearities.



#### 20.2c.2 Complex Geometries and Configurations



Another challenge in using plane-motion kinematics is dealing with complex geometries and configurations of the system. In real-world applications, systems can have multiple degrees of freedom and complex geometries, making it difficult to accurately model their dynamics using simple kinematic equations.



To overcome this challenge, advanced techniques such as multibody dynamics and finite element analysis can be used. Multibody dynamics involves modeling the system as a collection of interconnected rigid bodies, allowing for a more accurate representation of its dynamics. Finite element analysis, on the other hand, involves dividing the system into smaller elements and using numerical methods to solve for the motion of each element, taking into account its complex geometry.



#### 20.2c.3 Uncertainties in Parameters and Initial Conditions



Finally, another challenge in using plane-motion kinematics is dealing with uncertainties in the parameters and initial conditions of the system. In real-world applications, it is often difficult to accurately measure or determine these values, leading to errors in the model and predictions.



To address this challenge, sensitivity analysis and robust control techniques can be used. Sensitivity analysis involves studying the effect of uncertainties in the parameters and initial conditions on the behavior of the system. Robust control techniques, on the other hand, involve designing control systems that can handle these uncertainties and still maintain stability and performance.



In conclusion, while plane-motion kinematics is a powerful tool for analyzing and modeling the dynamics of two-degree-of-freedom systems, it is not without its challenges. By understanding and addressing these challenges, we can create more accurate and reliable models that can be used in a wide range of applications.





# Title: Modeling Dynamics and Control II:



## Chapter 20: Vibrations of Two-Degree-of-Freedom Systems:



### Section: 20.3 Plane-motion Dynamics of Rigid Bodies:



### Subsection (optional): 20.3a Understanding Plane-motion Dynamics



In the previous section, we discussed the basics of plane-motion kinematics and its applications in understanding the behavior of two-degree-of-freedom systems. Now, we will delve into the dynamics of these systems and how they can be modeled using plane-motion dynamics of rigid bodies.



#### 20.3a.1 Equations of Motion for Two-Degree-of-Freedom Systems



To understand the dynamics of two-degree-of-freedom systems, we must first establish the equations of motion for these systems. These equations are derived from the principles of Newtonian mechanics and are essential in understanding the behavior of the system.



The equations of motion for a two-degree-of-freedom system can be written as:



$$

M\ddot{\mathbf{x}} + C\dot{\mathbf{x}} + K\mathbf{x} = \mathbf{F}

$$



where $M$ is the mass matrix, $C$ is the damping matrix, $K$ is the stiffness matrix, $\mathbf{x}$ is the vector of generalized coordinates, and $\mathbf{F}$ is the vector of external forces.



#### 20.3a.2 Solving the Equations of Motion



Solving the equations of motion for a two-degree-of-freedom system can be a challenging task, especially when dealing with nonlinearities and complex geometries. However, there are various techniques that can be used to solve these equations and obtain the system's response.



One such technique is the method of modal analysis, which involves decomposing the system into its natural modes of vibration and solving for the response of each mode. This method is particularly useful for linear systems with simple geometries.



For more complex systems, numerical methods such as the finite element method can be used. This method involves dividing the system into smaller elements and solving for the response of each element, which is then combined to obtain the overall system response.



#### 20.3a.3 Challenges in Modeling Plane-motion Dynamics



Similar to the challenges faced in plane-motion kinematics, there are also challenges in modeling the dynamics of two-degree-of-freedom systems using plane-motion dynamics. These challenges include nonlinearities, complex geometries, and the need for accurate and efficient numerical methods.



To overcome these challenges, it is important to carefully consider the assumptions and simplifications made in the modeling process and to use appropriate techniques to address nonlinearities and complex geometries. Additionally, advancements in computational tools and techniques have made it easier to accurately model and analyze the dynamics of these systems.



In the next section, we will explore the concept of vibrations in two-degree-of-freedom systems and how they can be analyzed and controlled using the principles of dynamics and control.





# Title: Modeling Dynamics and Control II:



## Chapter 20: Vibrations of Two-Degree-of-Freedom Systems:



### Section: 20.3 Plane-motion Dynamics of Rigid Bodies:



### Subsection (optional): 20.3b Applications of Plane-motion Dynamics



In the previous section, we discussed the basics of plane-motion dynamics of rigid bodies and how they can be used to model the behavior of two-degree-of-freedom systems. Now, we will explore some of the applications of this concept in various fields.



#### 20.3b.1 Aerospace Engineering



One of the most significant applications of plane-motion dynamics is in the field of aerospace engineering. The motion of aircraft, spacecraft, and other flying objects can be modeled using the principles of plane-motion dynamics. This allows engineers to predict and control the behavior of these systems, ensuring their safety and efficiency.



For example, the rotation of a spacecraft in orbit can be visualized using Poinsot's construction, which is based on the principles of plane-motion dynamics. This visualization is crucial in understanding the spacecraft's orientation and its stability in orbit.



#### 20.3b.2 Robotics



Another field where plane-motion dynamics plays a crucial role is robotics. The motion of robotic arms and other mechanical systems can be modeled using the equations of motion derived from plane-motion dynamics. This allows engineers to design and control these systems for various applications, such as manufacturing and automation.



#### 20.3b.3 Control Systems



The principles of plane-motion dynamics are also essential in the field of control systems. The equations of motion for two-degree-of-freedom systems can be used to design controllers that can regulate the system's behavior and response. This is particularly useful in systems that require precise and stable control, such as industrial machinery and vehicles.



#### 20.3b.4 Biomechanics



In the field of biomechanics, plane-motion dynamics is used to model the movement and behavior of human and animal bodies. By understanding the dynamics of these systems, researchers can gain insights into the mechanics of movement and develop treatments for injuries and disabilities.



#### 20.3b.5 Structural Engineering



The principles of plane-motion dynamics are also applied in structural engineering to analyze and design buildings, bridges, and other structures. By modeling the behavior of these structures using the equations of motion, engineers can ensure their stability and safety under various loading conditions.



In conclusion, the applications of plane-motion dynamics are vast and diverse, making it a crucial concept in various fields of engineering and science. By understanding and utilizing this concept, we can gain insights into the behavior of complex systems and design solutions to control and optimize their performance.





# Title: Modeling Dynamics and Control II:



## Chapter 20: Vibrations of Two-Degree-of-Freedom Systems:



### Section: 20.3 Plane-motion Dynamics of Rigid Bodies:



### Subsection (optional): 20.3c Challenges in Plane-motion Dynamics



In the previous section, we discussed the basics of plane-motion dynamics of rigid bodies and how they can be used to model the behavior of two-degree-of-freedom systems. However, as with any mathematical model, there are certain challenges that must be addressed in order to accurately represent real-world systems. In this subsection, we will explore some of the challenges that arise in plane-motion dynamics and how they can be overcome.



#### 20.3c.1 Nonlinearities



One of the main challenges in plane-motion dynamics is the presence of nonlinearities in the system. Nonlinearities can arise from various sources, such as friction, damping, and external forces. These nonlinearities can significantly affect the behavior of the system and make it difficult to accurately predict its motion.



To overcome this challenge, various techniques have been developed, such as linearization and numerical methods. Linearization involves approximating the nonlinear equations of motion with linear equations, which can be solved using standard techniques. Numerical methods, on the other hand, involve using computer algorithms to solve the nonlinear equations of motion directly. Both of these methods have their advantages and limitations, and the choice of method depends on the specific system being modeled.



#### 20.3c.2 Uncertainties



Another challenge in plane-motion dynamics is dealing with uncertainties in the system. Uncertainties can arise from various sources, such as measurement errors, modeling errors, and external disturbances. These uncertainties can significantly affect the accuracy of the model and make it difficult to predict the behavior of the system.



To address this challenge, various techniques have been developed, such as robust control and adaptive control. Robust control involves designing controllers that can handle uncertainties and disturbances in the system. Adaptive control, on the other hand, involves continuously updating the model based on new information to improve its accuracy. Both of these techniques have been successfully applied in various fields, such as aerospace engineering and robotics.



#### 20.3c.3 Coupling Effects



In some systems, the motion of one degree of freedom can affect the motion of the other degree of freedom. This is known as coupling effects and can significantly complicate the equations of motion. These effects can arise from various sources, such as structural flexibility and external forces.



To address this challenge, various techniques have been developed, such as modal analysis and decoupling methods. Modal analysis involves decomposing the system into its individual modes of vibration, which can then be analyzed separately. Decoupling methods involve designing controllers that can decouple the two degrees of freedom, allowing for independent control of each degree of freedom. Both of these techniques have been successfully applied in various fields, such as control systems and biomechanics.



In conclusion, while plane-motion dynamics provides a powerful tool for modeling the behavior of two-degree-of-freedom systems, it is important to be aware of the challenges that can arise and the techniques that can be used to overcome them. By understanding and addressing these challenges, we can create more accurate and reliable models that can be applied in a wide range of fields, from aerospace engineering to biomechanics.
